  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2a750060-eaae-426c-9d03-740ac6a2f4ee'

<span id="freeTextContainer3870263114766809480"><b>From the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Giver of Stars</i>, in an earlier work available in the U.S. for the first time, a post-WWII story of the war brides who crossed the seas by the thousands to face their unknown futures.</b><br/><br/>1946. World War II has ended and all over the world, young women are beginning to fulfill the promises made to the men they wed in wartime.<br/><br/> In S</span>
  <span id="freeText3870263114766809480" style="display:none"><b>From the <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Giver of Stars</i>, in an earlier work available in the U.S. for the first time, a post-WWII story of the war brides who crossed the seas by the thousands to face their unknown futures.</b><br /><br />1946. World War II has ended and all over the world, young women are beginning to fulfill the promises made to the men they wed in wartime.<br /><br /> In Sydney, Australia, four women join 650 other war brides on an extraordinary voyage to England—aboard HMS <i>Victoria</i>, which still carries not just arms and aircraft but a thousand naval officers. Rules are strictly enforced, from the aircraft carrier’s captain down to the lowliest young deckhand. But the men and the brides will find their lives intertwined despite the Navy’s ironclad sanctions. And for Frances Mackenzie, the complicated young woman whose past comes back to haunt her far from home, the journey will change her life in ways she never could have predicted—forever.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3870263114766809480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/33657308-kelliann-gomez"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1599276376i/33657308._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/33657308-kelliann-gomez">Kelliann Gomez</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    Having been a Marine, you are known by your last name and last name only really in the military. People who call you by your first name are generally <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    Having been a Marine, you are known by your last name and last name only really in the military. People who call you by your first name are generally much closer to you and know you more as a regular person than as a military member. He was Nicol or "Marine" throughout the entire book. Frances only knew him as "Marine" for most of the book, not even by his last name, so telling Frances to call him "Henry" was letting her into that bubble of knowing him as a person while also introducing himself to her (as opposed to Highfield telling her his surname), not as Nicol the Marine and also showing the transition to starting over in civilian life after the war and loving again after his divorce.<br />At least that was my interpretation.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    My take on that is that he just hadn't found out about the dog at that particular moment. For me, his mentioning the dog was a way for us to see that <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    My take on that is that he just hadn't found out about the dog at that particular moment. For me, his mentioning the dog was a way for us to see that he was a kind man, not at all the stiff officer he seemed to be through most of the book. <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2473210287" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer16075916031120926678">I don't think I would have picked this up by myself (the synopsis didn't sound all too exciting to me), but I got the book gifted to me by someone who knows how much I loved <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17347634.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_' title='Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Me Before You</a>. I definitely need to remember to give this person a massive 'Thank you!' now!<br/>I was majorly surprised by how interesting I found the entire journey. The plot is very linear, there are no big surprises or plot twists. However, I was still glued to the pages due to the wonderful and realistic characters. I fell i</span>
  <span id="freeText16075916031120926678" style="display:none">I don't think I would have picked this up by myself (the synopsis didn't sound all too exciting to me), but I got the book gifted to me by someone who knows how much I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17347634.Me_Before_You__Me_Before_You___1_" title="Me Before You (Me Before You, #1) by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Me Before You</a>. I definitely need to remember to give this person a massive 'Thank you!' now!<br />I was majorly surprised by how interesting I found the entire journey. The plot is very linear, there are no big surprises or plot twists. However, I was still glued to the pages due to the wonderful and realistic characters. I fell in love with them and wanted to find out more and more about them. <br />I can't say that this was the <i>best</i> book ever or anything special, but I don't have a single complaint either, which is why I simply cannot give less than five stars. This is a perfect book to read in-between, when you just need to read something light and easy to relax for a bit.</span>

<div id="review_1097511021" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097511021" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1277905205p2/1166663.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1097511021?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/1166663-carol">Carol</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1166663-carol?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097511021" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8974188541987931637">Maybe this leopard can change her spots. I'm the perennial thriller reader. I read thrillers because they are often fast passed, make my heart beat faster and I love a suspenseful read. So why have I found myself bewtiched by the author JoJo Moyes? I have just finished my third book <u>The Ship of Brides</u> and will be singing its praises to everyone I meet.<br/> <br/>It’s the end of World War II and thousands of Australian women, War Brides, will be traveling to England to reunite with the men they married. Ov</span>
  <span id="freeText8974188541987931637" style="display:none">Maybe this leopard can change her spots. I'm the perennial thriller reader. I read thrillers because they are often fast passed, make my heart beat faster and I love a suspenseful read. So why have I found myself bewtiched by the author JoJo Moyes? I have just finished my third book <u>The Ship of Brides</u> and will be singing its praises to everyone I meet.<br /> <br />It’s the end of World War II and thousands of Australian women, War Brides, will be traveling to England to reunite with the men they married. Over 600 will not have the luxury of traveling on a ship like the Queen Mary with all of its amenities, but will make the six week journey on The Victoria, an aircraft carrier. The Victoria is ill suited as a vessel for women, outfitted for its crew of men and planes. The book focuses on four of the brides allowing us a window to their hopes, fears and dreams. These four along with the others are leaving all that they know, all who they know behind to start a new life on foreign shores. Even those madly in love wonder at the sanity of their decision. And what of those who mid-voyage receive a sort of Dear Jane letter, one stating <br /><br />What I really liked about  <u>The Ship of Brides</u> is how it made me think. I started to wonder about the women and ship the book is based on. How much fact, how much fiction? It took me on a new journey seeking answers. If you have any desire to know more about this slice of history three websites provided lots of information, the best being <a href="http://naa.gov.au/collection/a-z/war-brides.aspx" rel="nofollow noopener">The National Archives of Australia</a>. These also were worth scouting out <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/HMS_Victorious_%28R38%29" rel="nofollow noopener">HMS Victorious</a>, <a href="http://archiver.rootsweb.ancestry.com/th/read/WARBRIDES/2007-04/1175545694" rel="nofollow noopener">Rootsweb Warbrides</a>. In addition it brought me back to memories of the war and how it affected my family. I am a baby boomer who wishes I asked more questions about their experiences leading up to, during and after the war before I lost all those who could answer. <br /><u>The Ship of Brides</u> held my attention from start to finish. I have become a fan of JoJo Moyes all over again. I'm so glad I haven't read all her books yet. This is something to truly look forward to. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8974188541987931637" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1097794958" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12213495615466705638"><b>2.5 Stars</b><p>This is my fifth Jojo Moyes novel and, unfortunately, the <i>only</i> one I thought would never end.</p><p>The storyline is <i>GREAT</i> based on actual historical events of post WW2 war brides traveling aboard a naval warship to reunite with their husbands in England. I also enjoyed reading the newspaper and journal entries posted at the beginning of each chapter, but other than Frances' and Nicol's story, I am sorry to say, it was pretty much slow going with confusing dialogue and needless <i>catty</i> conversat</p></span>
  <span id="freeText12213495615466705638" style="display:none"><b>2.5 Stars</b><p>This is my fifth Jojo Moyes novel and, unfortunately, the <i>only</i> one I thought would never end.</p><p>The storyline is <i>GREAT</i> based on actual historical events of post WW2 war brides traveling aboard a naval warship to reunite with their husbands in England. I also enjoyed reading the newspaper and journal entries posted at the beginning of each chapter, but other than Frances' and Nicol's story, I am sorry to say, it was pretty much slow going with confusing dialogue and needless <i>catty</i> conversations throughout a good portion of the book.</p><p>Cannot recommend <i>this</i> 2005 JJM novel, but enthusiastically look forward to future offerings.</p><p>Highly recommend: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15507958.Me_Before_You" title="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1357108762s/15507958.jpg" alt="Me Before You by Jojo Moyes" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10163292.The_Last_Letter_from_Your_Lover" title="The Last Letter from Your Lover by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1407411868s/10163292.jpg" alt="The Last Letter from Your Lover by Jojo Moyes" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17572903.The_Girl_You_Left_Behind" title="The Girl You Left Behind by Jojo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1366558957s/17572903.jpg" alt="The Girl You Left Behind by Jojo Moyes" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>.</p></span>

<div id="review_1150307578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1150307578" />
    <a title="Suzanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11889829-suzanne"><img alt="Suzanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593566451p2/11889829.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1150307578?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Suzanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Suzanne" href="/user/show/11889829-suzanne">Suzanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340830116" href="/book/show/1172548.The_Ship_of_Brides">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11889829-suzanne?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11889829-suzanne?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1150307578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5953556926542517294">What a wonderful book that I've just finished. One of those that really mean something. It was a pleasure to read this book, the first of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8445471.Jo_Jo_Moyes' title='Jo Jo Moyes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jo Jo Moyes</a> that I have had the pleasure to read. This is a beautiful story that is based on a factual voyage, each chapter starts with an non fictional extract based on experiences of war brides, or those who served on the 'Victorious'.<br/><br/>The year is 1946, and almost 700 war brides are making their way to England, the war is over. We follow a group of gals who h</span>
  <span id="freeText5953556926542517294" style="display:none">What a wonderful book that I've just finished. One of those that really mean something. It was a pleasure to read this book, the first of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8445471.Jo_Jo_Moyes" title="Jo Jo Moyes" rel="nofollow noopener">Jo Jo Moyes</a> that I have had the pleasure to read. This is a beautiful story that is based on a factual voyage, each chapter starts with an non fictional extract based on experiences of war brides, or those who served on the 'Victorious'.<br /><br />The year is 1946, and almost 700 war brides are making their way to England, the war is over. We follow a group of gals who have so many stories to tell. Maggie - feisty girl of the land. Lovely. Avice - society girl, vein and focused on things not so important. Annoying. My favourite (just!) Frances - capable nurse who has survived a horrible upbringing. A treasure. <br /><br />We learn about life on board in trying times, and the crew that is charged with getting our brides there safe and sound. I also enjoyed the character of the captain, and Henry too.<br /><br />I've always enjoyed and appreciated a book that educates me, and this really did. This should be read by students as well, there's a true story amongst the happy and sad moments. The poor brides who received a telegram 'Not wanted, don't come'. Heart breaking.<br /><br />Please do read this, highly recommended by this Aussie girl who has learnt a lot. Hats off to Ms Moyes for not just a novel, but a thoroughly researched piece of work. A perfect holiday read. I will think about this a lot, it's gotten to me!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5953556926542517294" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/834297405" />
    <a title="Buggy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3099666-buggy"><img alt="Buggy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1289702969p2/3099666.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/834297405?book_show_action=true">Jan 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Buggy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Buggy" href="/user/show/3099666-buggy">Buggy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=high-seas-rom">high-seas-rom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=shelf-14">shelf-14</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=hist-rom">hist-rom</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=men-in-uniform-af-spc-op">men-in-uniform-af-spc-op</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=multiple-pov">multiple-pov</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3099666-buggy?shelf=australia">australia</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer834297405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3506420294006475198">Opening Line: <i>“The first time I saw her again, I felt as if I’d been hit.”</i><br/><br/>I absolutely loved this book, another winner from JoJo Moyes who bases this moving story on real events (and her own grandmother) Taking the reader back to 1946 in the aftermath of the Second World War as thousands of young war brides are transported from Australia to England to meet up with their GI husbands who they’d married during the conflict. For many woman it was a time of huge uncertainty, leaving their families an</span>
  <span id="freeText3506420294006475198" style="display:none">Opening Line: <i>“The first time I saw her again, I felt as if I’d been hit.”</i><br /><br />I absolutely loved this book, another winner from JoJo Moyes who bases this moving story on real events (and her own grandmother) Taking the reader back to 1946 in the aftermath of the Second World War as thousands of young war brides are transported from Australia to England to meet up with their GI husbands who they’d married during the conflict. For many woman it was a time of huge uncertainty, leaving their families and everything they’d ever known behind and preying they didn’t receive the dreaded “Not wanted, don’t come telegram” once aboard.<br /><br />Ship Of Brides follows four of these woman (out of the 650 on board) all from very different backgrounds and covers their experience from a boarding house in Sydney throughout their 6 week journey at sea aboard an aircraft carrier (which also still carries over a thousand naval officers so rules of honor, duty and separation must be enforced.<br /><br />The story begins in India in 2002 (which initially threw me a bit) as an elderly grandmother on vacation stumbles across the broken hull of a once great British warship, now in the process of being dismantled for scrap on an oily, debris littered beach. She has come upon a ship graveyard and can just make out the name on one of the rusted hulls “Victoria” and at once is overwhelmed by memories…<br /><br />I was surprised by how involved I got in this story but Moyes not only takes the reader back to 1946 but manages to keep a huge element of suspense going throughout the journey (Frances, a former nurse is kept frustratingly mysterious until the very last pages – and I kinda loved her.) We also enter the POV of the injured and grieving Captain, a Marine who has received a Dear John letter, a woman widowed before she reaches her destination, another who discovers her husband is already married and follow stowaway dogs, boiler room brawls, disastrous fires, miscarriages, lovely leg contests, ashore days in India and Gibraltar, excitement, fear, heartache and joy. <br /><br />Because this has been based on an actual sailing taken by the HMS Victorious, Moyes was able to include extracts from journals, newspaper clippings, and diary entries from the actual men and women aboard which added an element of real emotion to the voyage.<br /><br />The writing is fantastic and by the end I felt like I really knew these women and wondered how their lives had turned out, in fact I didn’t want to let them go.<br /><br />401jb5</span>
  <a data-text-id="3506420294006475198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_937276693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/937276693" />
    <a title="Tara Chevrestt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2544368-tara-chevrestt"><img alt="Tara Chevrestt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399003936p2/2544368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/937276693?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tara Chevrestt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tara Chevrestt" href="/user/show/2544368-tara-chevrestt">Tara Chevrestt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/20510869-the-ship-of-brides">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=good-writers">good-writers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2544368-tara-chevrestt?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer937276693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8776152846848388234">I'm a huge fan of Jojo Moyes and until now have never been on the fence with what to rate her work. This one is a tough one though. I liked half; I disliked half. I found myself impatient to know what happened in the end, to each and every one of the girls, yet at the same time, I found myself skimming the "man" parts--the captain's tale, Nicol's story, this guy and that guy. They bored me, and I didn't care about their lives.<br/><br/>This story doesn't really let the reader get to know the heroines, and</span>
  <span id="freeText8776152846848388234" style="display:none">I'm a huge fan of Jojo Moyes and until now have never been on the fence with what to rate her work. This one is a tough one though. I liked half; I disliked half. I found myself impatient to know what happened in the end, to each and every one of the girls, yet at the same time, I found myself skimming the "man" parts--the captain's tale, Nicol's story, this guy and that guy. They bored me, and I didn't care about their lives.<br /><br />This story doesn't really let the reader get to know the heroines, and there are four, at least not until the very end. It felt almost like each of the heroines was being held back from us, preventing the reader from being in anyone's head, heart, or experiencing their full range of emotions, and I prefer to be completely one with the character, so this method of not letting us know who these women really are until the last 15% doesn't work well for me.<br /><br />And why, oh why, did there even have to be a dog if it's going to end like that??????<br /><br />But I was fascinated by the story itself, by the fact all these brides are shoved together on an aircraft carrier for six weeks, by the fact that the captain pushed aircraft overboard, appalled by the behavior of some drunken seamen, even more shocked at the unfortunate "Not Wanted Don't Comes". Can't imagine how embarrassing that is...<br /><br />Even more mind boggling was the fact that many of these women on the ship were leaving everything (Australia) and everyone they'd ever known to go to a country (England) they'd never been before to be with men they'd married yet barely knew, and some of them are eight months pregnant and their husbands are about to lay eyes on women whom were young, thin beauties last they saw them..for their few days or weeks of marriage. It's crazy how rashly people acted during the war. And we see with some of these women that rashness comes back to bite them.<br /><br />There was a lot of sadness in this story, as well as a lot of women overcoming all kinds of problems. My favorite character had to be Frances. She intrigued me the most though the book took too long to really let me "in there". In her story, we see how very quick people are to judge based on so little data and how important it is to know the full story.<br /><br />And amid all the sadness, secrets, harassment, betrayals, and worrying who'll get the next "Not Wanted Don't Come", there are surprise bursts of humor, which in my opinion, kept this book afloat.<br /><br />Find out what quotes made me chuckle the most: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://wwwbookbabe.blogspot.com/2014/08/shocking-secrets-and-surprise-bursts-of.html#.U9zhPvldVK0">http://wwwbookbabe.blogspot.com/2014/...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8776152846848388234" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer4349391476934911042">I love JoJo Moyes and her ability to make Chick-lit (which I love), just a bit different. Some of her books are based on historical events, again something that I find is a great asset to her writing.<br/>However, and it is a shame to say that, this book just didn't work for me. I found the storyline hard to get in to, possibly a little dull at times. I don't know much about the subject of Australian war brides and the book didn't really help. I found it hard to pick up on the love the brides had for</span>
  <span id="freeText4349391476934911042" style="display:none">I love JoJo Moyes and her ability to make Chick-lit (which I love), just a bit different. Some of her books are based on historical events, again something that I find is a great asset to her writing.<br />However, and it is a shame to say that, this book just didn't work for me. I found the storyline hard to get in to, possibly a little dull at times. I don't know much about the subject of Australian war brides and the book didn't really help. I found it hard to pick up on the love the brides had for their English husbands when we had no idea on their backgrounds.<br />I want to keep trying to get through this, I wouldn't recommend as the best book to get into JoJo Moyes. </span>

<div id="review_979372497" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/979372497" />
    <a title="(ツ) Hache" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9056424-hache"><img alt="(ツ) Hache" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518026241p2/9056424.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/979372497?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="(ツ) Hache" class="user" itemprop="url" name="(ツ) Hache" href="/user/show/9056424-hache">(ツ) Hache</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9056424-hache?shelf=world-war">world-war</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9056424-hache?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9056424-hache?shelf=jojo-moyes">jojo-moyes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer979372497" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1695338476761764054">Firstly I have to say that this is a tough book to get into. I put it down many times and only read little bits at a time, It almost felt like I was reading this for school. If it was by any other author I would've given up. I'm so glad I kept with it.<br/><br/>Once you actually read a meaty chuck of it you start to feel like your really on board the ship apart of these brides lives. <br/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>Characters/POV</u>
</b><br/><br/>Told in third person narrative, there a 4 main brides out of the 650 women who end up being roomies toget</span>
  <span id="freeText1695338476761764054" style="display:none">Firstly I have to say that this is a tough book to get into. I put it down many times and only read little bits at a time, It almost felt like I was reading this for school. If it was by any other author I would've given up. I'm so glad I kept with it.<br /><br />Once you actually read a meaty chuck of it you start to feel like your really on board the ship apart of these brides lives. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Characters/POV</u>
</b><br /><br />Told in third person narrative, there a 4 main brides out of the 650 women who end up being roomies together.<br /><br /><b>Margaret</b> - A farm girl who's heavily pregnant.<br /><br /><b>Avice</b> - A society type, wealthy. Her pov is a bit snobby towards the other girls at times<br /><br /><b>Jean</b> - A 16 year old bride, chatty, drinks alot of alcohol which leads to her downfall. No pov from her.<br /><br /><b>Frances</b> - A nurse, quiet, like's to keep to herself, trying to escape her past. <br /><br />There's a mix of these 3 brides povs throughout the book, If I where to tell you who the main character is it would be a toss up between Margaret and Frances, there's more from Margaret in the first half and the second half we have more of Frances pov once we find out her past. If I were to spoil it for you I would say this is more <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Frances book <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Two other male characters povs that feature in this is the captain and a marine who stands guard outside the womens room.<br /><br />The second half and especially the last chapters of the book have more of the Marines pov<br /><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Romance</u>
</b><br /><br />The romance was a small part of the book, there's a very slow slow build up of romance between Frances and Nicol(Marine) and its more present towards the last quarter of the book. I absolutely loved this!!! you desperately want to know if they end up together. <br /><br /><br /><br />Most of the book takes place on board the ship in 1946 with the last part 2 chapter having them arrive in England. Part three only has one chapter which I guess is more of an Epilogue, that takes place back in 2002 where the book started from.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>Is this a sad book?</b><br />Not really, there a are things in the brides lives that happen on board that can be a bit sad, they all start off stepping aboard exited to be reunited with their husbands in the end...<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ only one of the brides is happily reunited with her husband. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />Although, once I got to chapter 26 and read 9 words I completely balled my eyes out.. I couldn't believe that 9 words could instantly bring me to tears. I actually took a bit of a brake and let the information sink in and had a really good cry. I realised I probably wasn't going to get my HEA. I forced myself to continue, crying along the way, those tears stopped and I started smiling, grinning, laughing, racing to the point where what I was crying over wasn't what I thought it was. I swear! my face hurt from all the emotions a felt during that last chapter!! OMG Author!! really?!! Incredible!<br /><br /><br />Lets just finish this off and say that this book <b>does have a very good HEA</b>. There's no epilogue but you do find out what happen to 3 of the brides. I would have liked to know what became of Jean though. But I'm happy with what I got. I think what made it more special was that the voyage was based on the real HMS Victorious, great to know about this piece of history.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1695338476761764054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18312673084493996774">I loved the idea of this book, but not the execution. I'm wondering if I built it up too much in my head before reading as I thought the premise a really interesting one. I enjoyed it but this book wasn't a favorite. Actually, that's the problem I have: this book read like a tv series. I feel like you could literally hand sections of the book to a director and, in order, he'll make an Avice episode, the Frances background episode, etc.<br/><br/>A quick, easy read with an interesting premise based on true </span>
  <span id="freeText18312673084493996774" style="display:none">I loved the idea of this book, but not the execution. I'm wondering if I built it up too much in my head before reading as I thought the premise a really interesting one. I enjoyed it but this book wasn't a favorite. Actually, that's the problem I have: this book read like a tv series. I feel like you could literally hand sections of the book to a director and, in order, he'll make an Avice episode, the Frances background episode, etc.<br /><br />A quick, easy read with an interesting premise based on true events. Good, but it feels like it could have been so much better. I would be interested in reading more of this author's work.</span>

They have either sustained my attention well enough or brought great enjoyment. I did not care for this one however. I just couldn't follow it, or relate. Neither could I develop care for the characters or the plot. Wasn't my cup of tea. Was more moved at the way it pulled together at the end. </span>

<div id="review_411355143" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/411355143" />
    <a title="Barbara Elsborg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2050186-barbara-elsborg"><img alt="Barbara Elsborg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498220836p2/2050186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/411355143?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barbara Elsborg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barbara Elsborg" href="/user/show/2050186-barbara-elsborg">Barbara Elsborg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer411355143" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11316047129575276904">I like Jojo Moyes but I'd avoided reading this one because of the time period. It's not something that interests me BUT what a mistake. I was quickly drawn in to the lives of these Australian women en route for the UK after the war as husbands of British servicemen. I loved the variety of characters, the understated love story, it all worked really well. I could easily see this as a film!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1920170929" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14878605664089528940">When I have bought and started to read this book (I confess) <b>I expected a few sweet romances in the package. What I got is much, much deeper and better.</b><br/><br/>5 stars for:<br/><br/><b>1) A original and very interesting historical background. I didn't know that such marriages were so much common during IIWW.<br/>2) Beautiful, gripping fictional stories.<br/>3) Perfectly chosen characters.<br/>4) A captivating, deep understanding of human nature.</b><br/><br/>There was moment (nearer the end) when I thought it was drifting to 4 stars. I felt a l</span>
  <span id="freeText14878605664089528940" style="display:none">When I have bought and started to read this book (I confess) <b>I expected a few sweet romances in the package. What I got is much, much deeper and better.</b><br><br>5 stars for:<br><br><b>1) A original and very interesting historical background. I didn't know that such marriages were so much common during IIWW.<br>2) Beautiful, gripping fictional stories.<br>3) Perfectly chosen characters.<br>4) A captivating, deep understanding of human nature.</b><br><br>There was moment (nearer the end) when I thought it was drifting to 4 stars. I felt a little lost, wanting that something else could happen. But the end improved everything. Yes, there was a happy ending! Yes, not for every of main characters but enough to feel warm closing the book.<br><br>I tell you, Frances, Margaret, Avice, Jean were magnificent persons, each one in her own way. Each one struggle with her own fears and past. <b>What happened to them before, during and after the voyage showed how different life and people are but at the same time how alike.</b> Next to female characters there were Nicol, Highfield, Tims and husbands. They presence made the book greater and more compelling. I can't tell you more about those people without spoiling, I am not able to do it (without spoiling) because their stories described and made them.<br><br>Really, it is almost hard to believe that Jojo Moyes chose so perfectly the stories which portrayed us, humans so aptly.<br><br>It isn't a light, cheerful book, but it isn't also a book which leave you crying. <b>I have finished it with the feeling that life can be difficult and painful but most people are good. They sometimes simply are in hard situations, make wrong decisions and so on. But there is happiness in life too!</b><br><br>Recommended reviews: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1097511021?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Carol's</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/979372497?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">(ツ) Hache's</a> - although her review will spoil you a few important things of the plot (I mean those not hidden).<br><br>[By the by, the cover of my copy is awful. In my opinion it doesn't fit at all. It suggest rather lighter, different book. Almost every other is better, except French and Dutch - they are even worse. I like a German cover the most.]<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495181586i/22793216.jpg" width="130" height="200" alt="Über uns der Himmel, unter uns das Meer" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="14878605664089528940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2273774490" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2273774490" />
    <a title="Jess The Bookworm" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32042916-jess-the-bookworm"><img alt="Jess The Bookworm" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1454940122p2/32042916.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2273774490?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess The Bookworm" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess The Bookworm" href="/user/show/32042916-jess-the-bookworm">Jess The Bookworm</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2273774490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10208378276555160327">3.5 stars.<br/><br/>This novel is set in the time period just after World War II. During the War many people from all over the world met one another and got married quite hastily, to people that they wouldn't see until the War was over. This novel starts off in Australia, where over 600 Australian brides need to be transported to their English husbands in England, to go and live as a married couple now that the War is over. <br/><br/>An old aircraft carrying ship is commissioned for its last journey to take these b</span>
  <span id="freeText10208378276555160327" style="display:none">3.5 stars.<br /><br />This novel is set in the time period just after World War II. During the War many people from all over the world met one another and got married quite hastily, to people that they wouldn't see until the War was over. This novel starts off in Australia, where over 600 Australian brides need to be transported to their English husbands in England, to go and live as a married couple now that the War is over. <br /><br />An old aircraft carrying ship is commissioned for its last journey to take these brides across the sea on the six week journey to be reunited with the loved one they haven't seen in months or even years. The author introduces us to four bunk mates, from very different walks of life, as they journey to their husbands. Some are from wealthy families, some are simple farm girls, some are young and naive, and some are hiding very dark pasts.<br /><br />This novel is based on a true story and on the real life 'ship of brides', the Vicorious, which carried brides from Australia to England after the War, and there are some real life journal extracts from that time scattered throughout the novel. What was really cool for me is that the author's grandmother was a bride on this ship, and she relayed her stories to her to enable her to write this book, and this is what made it special for me.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10208378276555160327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3341112583?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3341112583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17333332605706280742">In 1946 all over the world young women were crossing the seas to be reunited with their loved ones. In Sidney, 650 brides embarked the Victoria to join their husbands in London.<br/>The four main characters: Frances, Margaret, Avice and Jean will have their life completely changed by this experience.<br/><br/>The book is written in such a solemn way that it brings you right there in 1946 alongside the brides, you can sense their emotions through every page. <br/>The author has been brilliant while presenting the ch</span>
  <span id="freeText17333332605706280742" style="display:none">In 1946 all over the world young women were crossing the seas to be reunited with their loved ones. In Sidney, 650 brides embarked the Victoria to join their husbands in London.<br />The four main characters: Frances, Margaret, Avice and Jean will have their life completely changed by this experience.<br /><br />The book is written in such a solemn way that it brings you right there in 1946 alongside the brides, you can sense their emotions through every page. <br />The author has been brilliant while presenting the characters, 4 women each of them with different traits. Jean: young, energetic, sensitive and sometimes naive. Avice: more focused on the appearance than anything else.<br />Margaret: fearful of what being a mother means. And Frances (my favourite): strong, independent, courageous woman who doesn’t let her past define her. <br /><br />I absolutely loved this book, probably my second favourite written by Jojo Moyes and I highly recommend it to historical romance’s lovers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17333332605706280742" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2616618-erin?shelf=wwii">wwii</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2616618-erin?shelf=intelligent-chick-lit">intelligent-chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2616618-erin?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1100082754" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5788720214750235023">I found the premise of this book to be more compelling than the actual story. I love a good, big, historical fiction romance novel, and I love the fact that it was based on true events of the day. The book itself left much to be desired. It was so slow in the beginning. I read this on my kindle and was 53% through before I was actually interested in reading more. Throughout, I wanted to know more about the relationships with the brides and their husbands. The book was primarily based on the rela</span>
  <span id="freeText5788720214750235023" style="display:none">I found the premise of this book to be more compelling than the actual story. I love a good, big, historical fiction romance novel, and I love the fact that it was based on true events of the day. The book itself left much to be desired. It was so slow in the beginning. I read this on my kindle and was 53% through before I was actually interested in reading more. Throughout, I wanted to know more about the relationships with the brides and their husbands. The book was primarily based on the relationships they develop on board with the other brides. It wasn't until the very end of the book that many pieces of the story came together. This may be a great plot device for a thriller or mystery, but I found it more annoying than anything else. I don't like having to guess what the characters are thinking about. For example, the Captain's back story was excruciatingly slow to develop. I won't refer to the other back stories as it would spoil the story.<br /><br />I have really enjoyed other JoJo Moyes books and look forward to reading more in the future. This book just fell a bit short for me.<br /><br />One thing I did enjoy was learning many foreign Australian and British colloquial terms. I had to use the dictionary button many times to figure out what they were talking about!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5788720214750235023" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower" href="/user/show/29402776-the-bursting-bookshelf-of-a-wallflower">The Bursting Bookshelf of a Wallflower</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2498029961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12687300738207399006"><b>5 stars - Coup de coeur!</b><br/><br/>I have seen <i>Jojo Moyes' books</i> a million times in book stores and libraries and I must say that their beautiful covers are jumping straight into everybody's eyes. I am usually not reading the genre of books <i>Jojo Moyes</i> is writing, but I definitely decided to give this author a try when I read the blurb of this book and the many reviews saying that this story is different from what she usually writes. <br/><br/>I must say that I was pulled into <b>this amazing story</b> right from the start.</span>
  <span id="freeText12687300738207399006" style="display:none"><b>5 stars - Coup de coeur!</b><br /><br />I have seen <i>Jojo Moyes' books</i> a million times in book stores and libraries and I must say that their beautiful covers are jumping straight into everybody's eyes. I am usually not reading the genre of books <i>Jojo Moyes</i> is writing, but I definitely decided to give this author a try when I read the blurb of this book and the many reviews saying that this story is different from what she usually writes. <br /><br />I must say that I was pulled into <b>this amazing story</b> right from the start. The fate of all these women got to me and I just wanted to know more about them and how everything would end. I didn't think that the part on the ocean was too long, I <b>didn't feel bored one second</b>. It was perfect, the balance between all the characters and the different elements and the fact that we didn't know the exact fate of every woman on the ship just made it feel very realistic. It didn't bother me, that some strands of the story seemed unresolved e.g<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jean's fate after leaving the ship <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />The next time I get a chance to buy second hand books, I will definitely give another book of this author a chance - maybe the genre doesn't matter as much anymore.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_1137504159" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1137504159" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6751264-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319310056p2/6751264.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1137504159?book_show_action=true">Dec 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/6751264-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143126478" href="/book/show/20893485-the-ship-of-brides">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1137504159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12915387633082638439">On October 27, 1945 the HMS Victorious set off for the first of three trips to transport WWII servicemen and war brides. Jojo Moyes's own grandmother was one of those brides, traveling from Australia to England to be with her husband. According to the acknowledgements, her story and others inspired The Ship of Brides, which was originally released back in 2005 but has recently been reissued by Penguin.<br/><br/>The war has ended and out of the remaining war brides in Australia, Margaret, Avice, Jean, and </span>
  <span id="freeText12915387633082638439" style="display:none">On October 27, 1945 the HMS Victorious set off for the first of three trips to transport WWII servicemen and war brides. Jojo Moyes's own grandmother was one of those brides, traveling from Australia to England to be with her husband. According to the acknowledgements, her story and others inspired The Ship of Brides, which was originally released back in 2005 but has recently been reissued by Penguin.<br /><br />The war has ended and out of the remaining war brides in Australia, Margaret, Avice, Jean, and Frances have each been chosen to travel to England aboard HMS Victory in a push to reunite them with their husbands. They aren't the first to travel to England and they aren't the last, but they're the lucky ones who won't have to wait any longer. The four couldn't be more different from one another and yet they find themselves bunkmates on the newly outfitted aircraft carrier. Margaret is massively pregnant; Jean, at sixteen, is among the youngest on board; Frances, a former nurse, is quite closemouthed about her past; and Avice is a society girl who'd hoped for roommates of a different class. But they each have one thing in common: they've left behind everything they know to start a new life. <br /><br />Decades later, one of these women gets the shock of a lifetime when she stumbles upon a reminder of that fateful journey. <br /><br />I rather liked The Ship of Brides, and I really wasn't sure that I would at the start. Mainly because I'd looked forward to it for so long but never really felt I was in the right mood for it. But I forced myself to sit down with it one evening and soon found myself quite taken in by the story.<br /><br />This one is very different from the other titles I've read by Moyes thus far. To be honest, that was appealing at this stage as both One Plus One and Silver Bay had a lot of common elements between them. And while there is some of that in The Ship of Brides, the premise and the WWII setting couldn't have been more different!<br /><br />This was most definitely a piece of history that was fairly new to me. Not so much the war brides aspect but the fact that such a massive undertaking to deliver these women to their new homes had occurred. Moyes does a wonderful job blending in historical quotes from real men and women concerning the actual HMS Victorious mission, setting the scene mood of the novel quite nicely. Each of the characters came across as genuine in both emotion and setting, making it easy to imagine them as real people. Bringing the story forward to the present day was also a nice touch that added another layer of believability for me as the reader.<br /><br />Ship of Brides may not be what you've come to expect from Moyes but it is a wonderful historical read, perfect for anyone who enjoys WWII fiction.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12915387633082638439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_393869534" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/393869534" />
    <a title="Gee" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5170137-gee"><img alt="Gee" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346151425p2/5170137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/393869534?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gee" href="/user/show/5170137-gee">Gee</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780340830116" href="/book/show/1172548.The_Ship_of_Brides">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer393869534" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11631723349018143537">This was my second Jojo Moyes book, after reading and thoroughly enjoying 'The last letter from your lover'. <br/><br/>The Ship of Brides is a moving story based on a real events taking place in the immediate aftermath of the Second World War, as thousands of young women were transported to Great Britain or the United States from Australia to meet up with the GI-husbands they married when they were stationed in the country during the conflict. In many cases, these young women left their families and homes</span>
  <span id="freeText11631723349018143537" style="display:none">This was my second Jojo Moyes book, after reading and thoroughly enjoying 'The last letter from your lover'. <br /><br />The Ship of Brides is a moving story based on a real events taking place in the immediate aftermath of the Second World War, as thousands of young women were transported to Great Britain or the United States from Australia to meet up with the GI-husbands they married when they were stationed in the country during the conflict. In many cases, these young women left their families and homes behind to take a painfully long journey steaming across the oceans for weeks, heading to an uncertain life in a foreign country.<br /><br />Beginning on a beach/ship graveyard in present-day India, the broken hull of a warship being scrapped brings back unexpected and overwhelming memories for an elderly grandmother on holiday. We are then taken back to the days immediately post 1945 and a story centering on four very different young women who are thrown together in sleeping quarters aboard the soon-to-be-retired Royal Navy aircraft carrier HMS Victoria. Together with hundreds of other young women on the ship, they are travelling to England to meet again the men they married when stationed in Australia as the war raged in the Pacific. They're heading to a life and country that's foreign, meeting their new families for the first time - having left their own families and friends behind, they must adjust to a tense and cramped life aboard the ship as well as the all male crew which leads to incidents and encounters, both unfortunate and uplifting.<br /><br />Adding particular depth to the story is the fact that The Ship of Brides is based on an actual journey that took place in 1946 on board the HMS Victorious and many of the diary entries and journal records of some of the crew and passengers of that journey are included at the beginning of each chapter. This adds the real emotion of actual events to a tale that is nicely written by Moyes and is rich in human warmth. <br /><br />I really enjoy Jojo Moyes' writing and The Ship of Brides is a lovely and moving story. It reminded me again of the sacrifices and experiences of that extraordinary generation that fought the Second World War and built a new world in its aftermath, giving up so much and embarking on long and arduous journies to build a life we today simply take for granted. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11631723349018143537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

			<a class="actionLink" href="/topic/show/20086955-ship-of-brides">Ship of Brides</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('kW23y9Cs3dR3IPvLM0/YjiDOPk6nWK3jBaODZE7oNcZePlbtQfo3tsxnHdpDtRK9eMWsPlItsyWiL669ICHD8w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Jx/dCyJkcR6lgNsQfDo8N6F+sxRWUEKPKyO16DRyC6DoTDwtszKbfB7HPQEMwPYE+XUhZKMlXEmMr5gxWrv9lQ==')})
  }

Komisarz Kastor Grudziński musi sobie poradzić ze zmianami w komendzie wojewódzkiej, ale przede wszystkim przekonać swoich przełożonych, że potrzebne są nowe metody działania. Sposoby, z których korzystali do tej pory, nie wystarczą, aby rozbić zorganizowaną przestępczość. Zadania nie ułatwia mu nowa sprawa, która wiąże się z zabójstwami dzieci na terenie Krakowa.\n\nCzy komisarz poradzi sobie z nową rzeczywistością i czy wreszcie uda mu się jakoś ułożyć swoje życie <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10959775396897280138">Jojo Moyes is a British novelist.<br/><br/>Moyes studied at Royal Holloway, University of London. She won a bursary financed by The Independent newspaper to study journalism at City University and subsequently worked for <i>The Independent</i> for 10 years. In 2001 she became a full time novelist. <br/><br/>Moyes' novel <i>Foreign Fruit</i> won the Romantic Novelists' Association (RNA) Romantic Novel of the Year in 2004.<br/><br/>She is mar</span>
  <span id="freeText10959775396897280138" style="display:none">Jojo Moyes is a British novelist.<br /><br />Moyes studied at Royal Holloway, University of London. She won a bursary financed by The Independent newspaper to study journalism at City University and subsequently worked for <i>The Independent</i> for 10 years. In 2001 she became a full time novelist. <br /><br />Moyes' novel <i>Foreign Fruit</i> won the Romantic Novelists' Association (RNA) Romantic Novel of the Year in 2004.<br /><br />She is married to journalist Charles Arthur and has three children.</span>
